## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv/dt depends on position x (restoring force), velocity v (damping), and possibly time t (external driving). Classical nonlinear oscillator equations like Duffing, Van der Pol, and driven oscillators provide the structural templates.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (unforced): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping depending on position)
- Driven harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic external forcing)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (full Duffing with driving)
- Quintic nonlinearity: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (cubic velocity damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (Rayleigh-type nonlinear damping)
- Quadratic-cubic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 (asymmetric restoring force)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x (time-modulated stiffness)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * (v**2)**(-0.5) (mixed damping, effectively sign(v))
- Helmholtz-Duffing: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (asymmetric nonlinear oscillator with damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-symmetry restoring forces → use only odd powers of x (x, x**3, x**5) indicating symmetric potential wells
- Broken symmetry in potential → include even powers of x (x**2) indicating asymmetric restoring forces
- Self-sustained oscillations → velocity-dependent terms with sign changes, e.g., (1 - c*x**2)*v structure (Van der Pol type)
- Periodic external driving → additive sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms independent of state variables
- Parametric excitation → multiplicative coupling between trigonometric functions of t and state variables x or v
- Amplitude-dependent frequency → cubic position terms x**3 (Duffing-type hardening/softening springs)
- Nonlinear energy dissipation → odd powers of velocity (v**3, v*|v|) representing turbulent or nonlinear drag
- Conservative system test → if no explicit v or t dependence, the system is Hamiltonian with dv/dt = -dU/dx
- Limit cycle behavior → competing linear negative damping and nonlinear positive damping terms in v

GT: F0*sin(t) - beta*sin(x)*v - c0*beta*v - mu*(c1 - x**c2)*v - omega0**c3*x*exp(-Abs(x))
Candidate formulas: 50

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `-0.748*v*(1 - x²) - 0.378*v*sin(x) - 0.756*v - 3.87*x*exp(-|x|) + 0.265*sin(t)`

Let me expand this:
- `0.748*v*x² - 0.748*v - 0.378*v*sin(x) - 0.756*v - 3.87*x*exp(-|x|) + 0.265*sin(t)`
- `= -3.87*x*exp(-|x|) + 0.748*v*x² - 1.504*v - 0.378*v*sin(x) + 0.265*sin(t)`

The key terms are:
1. `x*exp(-|x|)` — a term involving x times exponential of -|x|
2. `v*x²` — v times x squared
3. `v` — linear in v
4. `v*sin(x)` — v times sin(x)
5. `sin(t)` — sine of t

The critical challenge is the `x*exp(-|x|)` term and the `v*sin(x)` term. These are transcendental functions that cannot be represented by polynomials or simple algebraic expressions.

Let me check each candidate for the ability to produce these terms:

**Term `x*exp(-|x|)`:** This is not a polynomial in x. None of the candidates have `exp(-|x|)` or `exp(f(x))` terms. The exponential terms in candidates are all `exp(c*t)`, which depend on t, not x.

**Term `v*sin(x)`:** This requires sin(x). None of the candidates contain `sin(x)`. The sin terms are all `sin(c*t + c)`, which depend on t, not x.

**Term `x*Abs(x)`:** Many candidates have this, but `x*|x|` is not the same as `x*exp(-|x|)`. For x > 0, `x*|x| = x²` while `x*exp(-|x|) = x*exp(-x)`. These are fundamentally different functions.

**Can we approximate?** No — we need exact equivalence for all values of x, t, v.

**Candidate 37 and 47:** These have terms like `v*(c8 + x)^c9` or `x*(c8 + v)^c9` which offer power-law flexibility but cannot produce `v*sin(x)` or `x*exp(-|x|)`.

**Candidate 40:** Has `x^c6` which is a power of x, not `x*exp(-|x|)`.

**Candidate 45:** Has `v^c6` which gives a power of v.

**Candidate 13:** Has `x^c9 * |v|` — still polynomial-type in x.

None of the candidates contain:
- Any function of x inside exp() (all exp terms are exp(c*t))
- Any sin(x) or cos(x) term (all trig terms are sin(c*t + c))

Since the GT requires both `x*exp(-|x|)` (which needs exp as a function of x) and `v*sin(x)` (which needs sin as a function of x), and no candidate has these functional forms, no candidate can match the GT.

Let me double-check: Could the `v*sin(x)` term combine with other v terms to form something representable? We have `-0.378*v*sin(x) - 1.504*v + 0.748*v*x²`. Factoring v out: `v*(-0.378*sin(x) - 1.504 + 0.748*x²)`. The expression in parentheses is a specific function of x that includes sin(x), which cannot be represented by polynomials or `x*|x|` type terms.

Similarly, `-3.87*x*exp(-|x|)` cannot be represented by any combination of `x`, `x*|x|`, `x²`, `x³`, `x⁵`, or other polynomial/algebraic terms available in the candidates.

No candidate can match the GT.
